## Load the libraries

```r
library(tidyverse)
library(janitor)
library(skimr)
```

For this assignment we are going to work with a large data set from the [United Nations Food and Agriculture Organization](http://www.fao.org/about/en/) on world fisheries. These data are pretty wild, so we need to do some cleaning. First, load the data.  

Load the data `FAO_1950to2012_111914.csv` as a new object titled `fisheries`.

```r
fisheries <- readr::read_csv(file = "data/FAO_1950to2012_111914.csv")
```

```

```

2. Use `janitor` to rename the columns and make them easier to use. As part of this cleaning step, change `country`, `isscaap_group_number`, `asfis_species_number`, and `fao_major_fishing_area` to data class factor. 

```r
fisheries <- janitor::clean_names(fisheries)
names(fisheries)
```

We need to deal with the years because they are being treated as characters and start with an X. We also have the problem that the column names that are years actually represent data. We haven't discussed tidy data yet, so here is some help. You should run this ugly chunk to transform the data for the rest of the homework. It will only work if you have used janitor to rename the variables in question 2!

```r
fisheries_tidy <- fisheries %>% 
  pivot_longer(-c(country,common_name,isscaap_group_number,isscaap_taxonomic_group,asfis_species_number,asfis_species_name,fao_major_fishing_area,measure),
              names_to = "year",
              values_to = "catch",
              values_drop_na = TRUE) %>%   mutate(year= as.numeric(str_replace(year, 'x', ''))) %>% 
  mutate(catch= str_replace(catch, c(' F'), replacement = '')) %>% 
  mutate(catch= str_replace(catch, c('...'), replacement = '')) %>% 
  mutate(catch= str_replace(catch, c('-'), replacement = '')) %>% 
  mutate(catch= str_replace(catch, c('0 0'), replacement = ''))

fisheries_tidy$catch <- as.numeric(fisheries_tidy$catch)
```

4. Refocus the data only to include country, isscaap_taxonomic_group, asfis_species_name, asfis_species_number, year, catch.

6. Which country had the largest overall catch in the year 2000?

```r
fisheries_tidy2%>%
  select(country, catch, year)%>%
  filter(year == 2000, catch >= 9000)
```

```
## # A tibble: 1 x 3
##   country catch  year
##   <chr>   <dbl> <dbl>
## 1 China    9068  2000
```
f%>% 
  arrange(desc(catch_total))
7. Which country caught the most sardines (_Sardina pilchardus_) between the years 1990-2000?

```r
fisheries_tidy2%>%
  select(country,asfis_species_name , year, catch)%>%
  filter( year>=1990 & year<=2000)%>%
  group_by(asfis_species_name == "Sadina pilchardus")%>%
  summarise(country)
```

```
## `summarise()` has grouped output by 'asfis_species_name == "Sadina pilchardus"'. You can override using the `.groups` argument.
```

```
## # A tibble: 84,944 x 2

##  2 FALSE                                       Albania
```

8. Which five countries caught the most cephalopods between 2008-2012?

```r
fisheries_tidy2%>%
  select(country, catch, asfis_species_name, year)%>%
  filter( year>=2008 & year<=2012)%>%
  group_by( country,asfis_species_name == "Cephalopod")%>%
  arrange(desc(catch))
```


9. Which species had the highest catch total between 2008-2012? (hint: Osteichthyes is not a species)

```r
fisheries_tidy2%>%
  filter(year>=2008 & year<= 2012)%>%
  group_by(asfis_species_name,isscaap_taxonomic_group)%>%
  summarise(biggest_catch=sum(catch, na.rm=T))%>%
  arrange(desc(biggest_catch))
```

```
## `summarise()` has grouped output by 'asfis_species_name'. You can override using the `.groups` argument.
```

10. Use the data to do at least one analysis of your choice.

```r
fisheries_tidy2%>%
  filter(year == 2001)%>%
  group_by(country=="United States", asfis_species_name)%>%
  summarise(USbiggestcatch = sum(catch, na.rm = T))%>%
  arrange(desc(USbiggestcatch))
```

```
## `summarise()` has grouped output by 'country == "United States"'. You can override using the `.groups` argument.
```

```

##  2 FALSE                        Trachurus murphyi              10774

##  7 FALSE                        Katsuwonus pelamis              5849
```
